match bash timeout exit code\n\n        self._close_handles()\n        return self._process.returncode if self._process.returncode is not None else -1\n\n    def terminate(self):\n        \"\"\"Graceful shutdown: SIGTERM, wait 10s, then SIGKILL.\"\"\"\n        if self._process is None or self._process.poll() is not None:\n            self._close_handles()\n            return\n\n        use_pgroup = all(hasattr(os, attr) for attr in (\"getpgid\", \"killpg\"))\n        pgid = os.getpgid(self._process.pid) if use_pgroup else None\n\n        # Phase 1: SIGTERM (group on Unix, process fallback otherwise)\n        try:\n            if use_pgroup and pgid is not None:\n                os.killpg(pgid, signal.SIGTERM)\n            else:\n                self._process.terminate()\n            debug_log(_dbg, \"signal_sent\", signal=\"SIGTERM\", pid=self._process.pid)\n        except ProcessLookupError:\n            self._close_handles()\n            return\n\n        # Phase 2: Wait up to 10 seconds\n        try:\n            self._process.wait(timeout=10)\n        except subprocess.TimeoutExpired:\n            # Phase 3: SIGKILL (group on Unix, process fallback otherwise)\n            try:\n                if use_pgroup and pgid is not None:\n                    os.killpg(pgid, signal.SIGKILL)\n                else:\n                    self._process.kill()\n                debug_log(_dbg, \"signal_sent\", signal=\"SIGKILL\", pid=self._process.pid)\n                self._process.wait(timeout=5)\n            except (ProcessLookupError, subprocess.TimeoutExpired):\n                pass\n\n        rc = self._process.returncode\n        debug_log(\n            _dbg,\n            \"exit\",\n            pid=self._process.pid,\n            code=rc,\n            was_timeout=(rc == 124 or getattr(self, \"_timed_out\", False)),\n        )\n        self._close_handles()\n\n    def _close_handles(self):\n        for fh in (self._stdout_fh, self._stderr_fh):\n            if fh is not None:\n                try:\n                    fh.close()\n                except Exception:\n                    pass\n\n\nclass SignalHandler:\n    \"\"\"Register signal handlers for graceful sprint shutdown.\n\n    On SIGINT/SIGTERM:\n    1. Set the shutdown flag (checked by the executor loop)\n    2. The executor terminates the current claude process\n    3. Writes partial execution log\n    4. Exits with appropriate code\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self):\n        self.shutdown_requested = False\n        self._original_sigint = None\n        self._original_sigterm = None\n\n    def install(self):\n        \"\"\"Install signal handlers.\"\"\"\n        self._original_sigint = signal.getsignal(signal.SIGINT)\n        self._original_sigterm = signal.getsignal(signal.SIGTERM)\n        signal.signal(signal.SIGINT, self._handle)\n        signal.signal(signal.SIGTERM, self._handle)\n\n    def uninstall(self):\n        \"\"\"Restore original signal handlers.\"\"\"\n        if self._original_sigint is not None:\n            signal.signal(signal.SIGINT, self._original_sigint)\n        if self._original_sigterm is not None:\n            signal.signal(signal.SIGTERM, self._original_sigterm)\n\n    def _handle(self, signum, frame):\n        self.shutdown_requested = True\n","numLines":251,"startLine":1,"totalLines":251}}}

Problem Statement\n    12→\n    13→The `/sc:roadmap` skill executes inside a single Claude Code context where all steps — extraction, variant generation, adversarial debate, merge — run as behavioral instructions within the same session. This makes fabrication structurally possible: Claude can skip expensive steps (e.g. actually invoking sc:adversarial-protocol) and self-report completion. The skill-to-skill invocation chain fails silently.\n    14→\n    15→**Root cause**: Claude controls its own workflow. Nothing external enforces step completion before the next step begins.\n    16→\n    17→**Solution**: A CLI command (`superclaude roadmap`) that acts as a conductor — calling Claude as a subprocess once per step, with a file-on-disk gate between each step. Claude cannot advance to step N+1 because the CLI hasn't issued that prompt yet. Fabrication becomes impossible without writing the required output files.\n    18→\n    19→<!-- Source: Variant B (tasklist-strategies), Strategy 1 rationale — merged per Change #3 -->\n    20→\n    21→**Design principle — no circular self-validation**: The conductor enforces a strict trust boundary. Gate validation (`gate_passed()`) is pure Python — it never invokes Claude to evaluate Claude's output. This eliminates the circular self-validation failure mode where the same model that produced an artifact judges its own quality, which produces false confidence regardless of how sophisticated the validation criteria are. The insight that \"the same model that produces output cannot reliably validate its own intermediate state\" (from adversarial analysis of tasklist pipeline strategies) is the architectural justification for externalizing all gate logic into deterministic Python.\n    22→\n    23→---\n    24→\n    25→## 2. Scope\n    26→\n    27→### In Scope (v1)\n    28→- `superclaude roadmap <spec-file>` CLI command\n    29→- 8-step pipeline (extract → generate-A/B in parallel → diff → debate → score → merge → test-strategy)\n    30→- Shared `pipeline/` base module extracted from `sprint/`\n    31→- Sprint migration to use `pipeline/` internals\n    32→- Gate validation: file existence + YAML frontmatter fields + minimum line count\n    33→- Retry-once-then-halt failure policy\n    34→- `--resume` flag for restarting from failed step\n    35→- `--dry-run` flag for plan preview\n    36→- Single PR delivery (pipeline/ extraction + sprint migration + roadmap/ all together)\n    37→\n    38→### Out of Scope (v1)\n    39→- TUI / rich progress display (stdout logging only)\n    40→- `--blind` adversarial mode flag\n    41→- Multi-spec consolidation (`--specs`)\n    42→- Tasklist generation from roadmap output\n    43→- `--agents` count > 2 (v1 supports exactly 2 agents for generate-A / generate-B)\n    44→\n    45→### 2.1 Design Constraints\n    46→<!-- Source: Variant B (tasklist-strategies), scope discipline — merged per Change #4 -->\n    47→\n    48→- **YAGNI enforcement**: The `pipeline/` module implements only patterns required by `sprint/` and `roadmap/`. No speculative abstractions for hypothetical future commands.\n    49→- **Conductor minimalism**: The conductor's responsibility is step sequencing, gate enforcement, retry logic, and state management. It does not interpret, evaluate, or transform artifact content.\n    50→- **No self-validation**: Gate checks are pure Python. The conductor never invokes Claude to judge Claude's output (see §1 design principle).\n    51→- **Deferral tracking**: Features considered and deferred are recorded in §11 with rationale, preserving decision provenance for future versions.\n    52→\n    53→---\n    54→\n    55→## 3. Architecture\n    56→\n    57→### 3.1 Module Structure\n    58→\n    59→```\n    60→src/superclaude/cli/\n    61→  pipeline/                  ← NEW: shared base, both sprint and roadmap extend it\n    62→    __init__.py\n    63→    process.py               ← ClaudeProcess (extracted from sprint/process.py; output_format parameterized: sprint=stream-json, roadmap=text)\n    64→    executor.py              ← execute_pipeline(): generic step sequencer\n    65→    models.py                ← PipelineConfig, Step, StepResult, StepStatus\n    66→    gates.py                 ← gate_passed() validator\n    67→  sprint/                    ← MIGRATED: imports from pipeline/ instead of owning logic\n    68→    __init__.py\n    69→    commands.py              ← unchanged external API\n    70→    config.py                ← SprintConfig extends PipelineConfig (new inheritance)\n    71→    executor.py              ← execute_sprint() wraps execute_pipeline()\n    72→    models.py                ← SprintStep extends Step; PhaseResult extends StepResult\n    73→    process.py               ← re-exports ClaudeProcess from pipeline.process\n    74→    monitor.py               ← unchanged\n    75→    tui.py                   ← unchanged\n    76→    tmux.py                  ← unchanged\n    77→    logging_.py              ← unchanged\n    78→    notify.py                ← unchanged\n    79→    # Also in sprint/ (NOT extracted): debug_logger.py, diagnostics.py\n    80→  roadmap/                   ← NEW\n    81→    __init__.py\n    82→    commands.py              ← Click entry point; registered in main.py\n    83→    models.py                ← RoadmapConfig extends PipelineConfig; RoadmapStep extends Step\n    84→    prompts.py               ← per-step prompt builders (pure functions, no I/O)\n    85→    gates.py                 ← roadmap gate definitions (data, not logic)\n    86→    executor.py              ← execute_roadmap() wraps execute_pipeline()\n    87→```\n    88→\n    89→### 3.2 `pipeline/` Interface Contract\n    90→\n    91→`PipelineConfig` — fields shared by both sprint and roadmap:\n    92→\n    93→```python\n    94→@dataclass\n    95→class PipelineConfig:\n    96→    work_dir: Path          # e.g. \"extract\", \"generate-opus\", \"diff\"\n   121→    prompt: str              # full prompt text passed to claude -p\n   122→    output_file: Path        # gate checks this file\n   123→    gate: GateCriteria       # what constitutes a passing output\n   124→    timeout_seconds: int     # hard timeout for this step's subprocess\n   125→    inputs: list[Path]       # files this step reads (injected into prompt context)\n   126→    retry_limit: int = 1     # default: retry once on gate failure\n   127→```\n   128→\n   129→`StepResult`:\n   130→\n   131→```python\n   132→@dataclass\n   133→class StepResult:\n   134→    step: Step\n   135→    status: StepStatus       # PASS | FAIL | TIMEOUT | SKIPPED\n   136→    attempt: int             # 1 or 2 (retry)\n   137→    gate_failure_reason: str | None   # populated on FAIL\n   138→    started_at: datetime\n   139→    finished_at: datetime\n   140→```\n   141→\n   142→`SemanticCheck`:\n   143→<!-- Source: Variant B, Strategies 3+4+5 — merged per Change #2 -->\n   144→\n   145→```python\n   146→@dataclass\n   147→class SemanticCheck:\n   148→    \"\"\"Pure Python check applied to file content. No LLM invocation.\"\"\"\n   149→    name: str                           # e.g. \"no_heading_gaps\"\n   150→    check_fn: Callable[[str], bool]     # receives file content, returns pass/fail\n   151→    failure_message: str                # human-readable on failure\n   152→```\n   153→\n   154→`GateCriteria`:\n   155→\n   156→```python\n   157→@dataclass\n   158→class GateCriteria:\n   159→    required_frontmatter_fields: list[str]\n   160→    min_lines: int\n   161→    enforcement_tier: Literal[\"STRICT\", \"STANDARD\", \"LIGHT\", \"EXEMPT\"] = \"STANDARD\"\n   162→    semantic_checks: list[SemanticCheck] | None = None\n   163→```\n   164→\n   165→`gate_passed()` in `pipeline/gates.py`:\n   166→\n   167→```python\n   168→def gate_passed(output_file: Path, criteria: GateCriteria) -> tuple[bool, str | None]:\n   169→    \"\"\"\n   170→    Returns (True, None) on pass.\n   171→    Returns (False, reason) on failure where reason is a human-readable message.\n   172→\n   173→    Validation is tier-proportional (see §3.3 Gate Enforcement Tiers):\n   174→    - EXEMPT: always passes\n   175→    - LIGHT: file exists + non-empty\n   176→    - STANDARD: file exists + non-empty + min lines + frontmatter fields\n   177→    - STRICT: all STANDARD checks + semantic checks (if defined)\n   178→\n   179→    Failure reasons:\n   180→    - \"File not found: {path}\"\n   181→    - \"File empty (0 bytes): {path}\"\n   182→    - \"Below minimum line count: {actual} < {required} in {path}\"\n   183→    - \"YAML frontmatter missing or unparseable in {path}: {parse_error}\"\n   184→    - \"Missing required frontmatter field '{field}' in {path}\"\n   185→    - \"Semantic check '{name}' failed: {failure_message}\"\n   186→    \"\"\"\n   187→```\n   188→\n   189→Note: `gate_passed()` is pure Python — no subprocess, no Claude invocation.\n   190→\n   191→### 3.3 Gate Enforcement Tiers\n   192→<!-- Source: Variant B (tasklist-strategies), Strategy 4 — merged per Change #1 -->\n   193→\n   194→Gate validation intensity is tier-proportional. PhaseResult extends StepResult\n    process.py               ← re-exports ClaudeProcess from pipeline.process\n    monitor.py               ← unchanged\n    tui.py                   ← unchanged\n    tmux.py                  ← unchanged\n    logging_.py              ← unchanged\n    notify.py                ← unchanged\n    # Also in sprint/ (NOT extracted): debug_logger.py, diagnostics.py\n  roadmap/                   ← NEW\n    __init__.py\n    commands.py              ← Click entry point; registered in main.py\n    models.py                ← RoadmapConfig extends PipelineConfig; RoadmapStep extends Step\n    prompts.py               ← per-step prompt builders (pure functions, no I/O)\n    gates.py                 ← roadmap gate definitions (data, not logic)\n    executor.py              ← execute_roadmap() wraps execute_pipeline()\n```\n\n### 3.2 `pipeline/` Interface Contract\n\n`PipelineConfig` — fields shared by both sprint and roadmap:\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass PipelineConfig:\n    work_dir: Path          # where output files are written\n    dry_run: bool = False\n    max_turns: int = 50     # passed to each claude -p subprocess\n    model: str = \"\"         # empty = claude default; accepts shorthand (opus/sonnet/haiku)\n    permission_flag: str = \"--dangerously-skip-permissions\"\n    debug: bool = False\n```\n\n`SprintConfig` retains sprint-specific fields (not in `PipelineConfig`):\n- `index_path`, `release_dir`, `phases`, `start_phase`, `end_phase`\n- `stall_timeout`, `stall_action`, `phase_timeout`\n- `tmux_session_name`\n\n`RoadmapConfig` adds roadmap-specific fields (not in `PipelineConfig`):\n- `spec_file: Path`\n- `agents: list[AgentSpec]`  (default: `[AgentSpec(\"opus\",\"architect\"), AgentSpec(\"haiku\",\"architect\")]`)\n- `depth: Literal[\"quick\",\"standard\",\"deep\"]`  (default: `\"standard\"`)\n- `output_dir: Path`  (default: parent dir of spec_file)\n\n`Step` — a single pipeline step:\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass Step:\n    id: str                  # e.g. \"extract\", \"generate-opus\", \"diff\"\n    prompt: str              # full prompt text passed to claude -p\n    output_file: Path        # gate checks this file\n    gate: GateCriteria       # what constitutes a passing output\n    timeout_seconds: int     # hard timeout for this step's subprocess\n    inputs: list[Path]       # files this step reads (injected into prompt context)\n    retry_limit: int = 1     # default: retry once on gate failure\n```\n\n`StepResult`:\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass StepResult:\n    step: Step\n    status: StepStatus       # PASS | FAIL | TIMEOUT | SKIPPED\n    attempt: int             # 1 or 2 (retry)\n    gate_failure_reason: str | None   # populated on FAIL\n    started_at: datetime\n    finished_at: datetime\n```\n\n`SemanticCheck`:\n<!-- Source: Variant B, Strategies 3+4+5 — merged per Change #2 -->\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass SemanticCheck:\n    \"\"\"Pure Python check applied to file content. No LLM invocation.\"\"\"\n    name: str                           # e.g. \"no_heading_gaps\"\n    check_fn: Callable[[str], bool]     # receives file content, returns pass/fail\n    failure_message: str                # human-readable on failure\n```\n\n`GateCriteria`:\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass GateCriteria:\n    required_frontmatter_fields: list[str]\n    min_lines: int\n    enforcement_tier: Literal[\"STRICT\", \"STANDARD\", \"LIGHT\", \"EXEMPT\"] = \"STANDARD\"\n    semantic_checks: list[SemanticCheck] | None = None\n```\n\n`gate_passed()` in `pipeline/gates.py`:\n\n```python\ndef gate_passed(output_file: Path, criteria: GateCriteria) -> tuple[bool, str | None]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Returns (True, None) on pass.\n    Returns (False, reason) on failure where reason is a human-readable message.\n\n    Validation is tier-proportional (see §3.3 Gate Enforcement Tiers):\n    - EXEMPT: always passes\n    - LIGHT: file exists + non-empty\n    - STANDARD: file exists + non-empty + min lines + frontmatter fields\n    - STRICT: all STANDARD checks + semantic checks (if defined)\n\n    Failure reasons:\n    - \"File not found: {path}\"\n    - \"File empty (0 bytes): {path}\"\n    - \"Below minimum line count: {actual} < {required} in {path}\"\n    - \"YAML frontmatter missing or unparseable in {path}: {parse_error}\"\n    - \"Missing required frontmatter field '{field}' in {path}\"\n    - \"Semantic check '{name}' failed: {failure_message}\"\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\nNote: `gate_passed()` is pure Python — no subprocess, no Claude invocation.\n\n### 3.3 Gate Enforcement Tiers\n<!-- Source: Variant B (tasklist-strategies), Strategy 4 — merged per Change #1 -->\n\nGate validation intensity is tier-proportional. Acceptance Criteria\n\nEnd-to-end acceptance tests (not unit tests — these validate the full CLI):\n\n**AC-01**: Given a valid spec-file, `superclaude roadmap spec.md --dry-run` prints 7 step entries (each with ID, output filename, gate criteria, timeout) and exits 0. No files written.\n\n**AC-02**: Given a valid spec-file, `superclaude roadmap spec.md` completes all 7 steps and writes 8 files to output-dir: `extraction.md`, `roadmap-opus-architect.md`, `roadmap-haiku-architect.md`, `diff-analysis.md`, `debate-transcript.md`, `base-selection.md`, `roadmap.md`, `test-strategy.md`.\n\n**AC-03**: Given a generate step that produces a file missing the `primary_persona` frontmatter field, the CLI retries once, then halts and prints the gate failure message containing the field name and file path. Exits non-zero.\n\n**AC-04**: Given a completed run (all gates pass), `superclaude roadmap spec.md --resume` prints `Skipping N steps (gates pass)` and exits 0 without launching any subprocesses.\n\n**AC-05**: Given a completed run followed by a spec-file modification, `superclaude roadmap spec.md --resume` detects the hash mismatch, prints the stale-spec warning, and re-runs the extract step.\n\n**AC-06**: `uv run pytest tests/sprint/` exits 0 after the pipeline/ migration (sprint external API unchanged).\n\n**AC-07**: `superclaude roadmap spec.md --agents sonnet:security,haiku:qa` uses `sonnet` and `haiku` as the model values in the two generate step subprocess invocations (verified via `--dry-run` output showing model per step).\n\n---\n\n## 11. Open Questions & Deferred Features\n\n| Question | Resolution |\n|----------|-----------|\n| Debate step granularity | 3 gated sub-steps: diff → debate → score (then merge as step 4) |\n| PR strategy | Single PR: pipeline/ extraction + sprint migration + roadmap/ |\n| Model shorthand resolution | Not needed — claude CLI accepts opus/sonnet/haiku natively |\n\n### Deferred Features (v1.1+)\n<!-- Source: Variant B (tasklist-strategies), v1.1 deferral table — merged per Change #6 -->\n\n| Feature | Considered In | Deferral Reason |\n|---------|--------------|-----------------|\n| Multi-spec consolidation (`--specs`) | §2 Out of Scope | Requires adversarial merge across >2 variants; validate 2-agent pipeline first |\n| `--blind` adversarial mode | §2 Out of Scope | Adds complexity without proven value in v1 |\n| >2 agents | §2 Out of Scope | v1 validates 2-agent pipeline before scaling |\n| TUI / rich progress display | §2 Out of Scope | stdout logging sufficient for v1; sprint TUI available for reference |\n| Tier-proportional semantic gates (full) | §3.3, this merge | Framework designed; full semantic check library deferred to v1.1 |\n| Content quality heuristics for input | Adversarial analysis | Duplicates parser logic; rejected per tasklist debate outcomes |\n| Per-step halt-on-failure with LLM validation | Adversarial analysis | Circular self-validation; external Python gates used instead |\n\n---\n\n## 12. Implementation Notes\n\n### Sprint Migration Strategy\n\nThe migration should not change any sprint behavior. Recommended approach:\n\n1. Create `pipeline/models.py` with `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `StepStatus`, `GateCriteria`\n2. Move `ClaudeProcess` from `sprint/process.py` to `pipeline/process.py`; re-export from `sprint/process.py`. Note: sprint/process.py contains `debug_log()` calls tied to sprint's debug logger. When extracting, replace with stdlib logging or remove (NFR-007 prohibits pipeline/ from importing sprint modules).\n3. Create `pipeline/executor.py` with `execute_pipeline()` as a generalized version of `execute_sprint()`\n4. Create `pipeline/gates.py` with `gate_passed()`\n5. Refactor `sprint/executor.py` to call `execute_pipeline()` internally\n6. Refactor `sprint/models.py`: `SprintConfig` inherits from `PipelineConfig`\n7. Run `uv run pytest tests/sprint/` — all tests must pass before proceeding to roadmap/ work\n8. Build `roadmap/` on top of the now-stable `pipeline/` base\n\n### Prompt Contract for Debate Sub-Steps\n\nEach of the three debate sub-steps (diff, debate, score) receives only the files listed in its `inputs` column. The debate step in particular must not receive the original spec-file — it operates only on the diff analysis and the two variant roadmaps. This is enforced by the executor's context isolation (FR-03).\n\n### `AgentSpec` Type\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass AgentSpec:\n    model: str      # e.g. \"opus\", \"sonnet\", \"haiku\"\n    persona: str    # e.g. \"architect\", \"security\", \"qa\"\n\n    @property\n    def id(self) -> str:\n        return f\"{self.model}-{self.persona}\"  # used in output filenames\n\n    @classmethod\n    def parse(cls, s: str) -> \"AgentSpec\":\n        \"\"\"Parse 'opus:architect' → AgentSpec(model='opus', persona='architect')\"\"\"\n        parts = s.split(\":\", 1)\n        model = parts[0].strip()\n        persona = parts[1].strip() if len(parts) > 1 else \"architect\"\n        return cls(model=model, persona=persona)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 13. Design & Architecture\n\n### 13.1 PipelineConfig Field Allocation\n\nThe extraction boundary is governed by one rule: **PipelineConfig owns fields that appear in `claude -p` subprocess invocation or control generic execution flow**. Sprint-specific orchestration (TUI, tmux, stall detection, phase numbering) stays in SprintConfig.\n\n| Field | PipelineConfig | SprintConfig | Rationale |\n|-------|:-:|:-:|-----------|\n| `work_dir: Path` | **✓** (new) | — | Both pipelines write output to a directory. Sprint sets this to `release_dir`; roadmap sets it to `output_dir`. |\n| `dry_run: bool` | **✓** | — | Both pipelines support `--dry-run`. |\n| `max_turns: int` | **✓** | — | Passed to `claude -p --max-turns` in both pipelines. |\n| `model: str` | **✓** | — | Passed to `claude -p --model` in both pipelines (roadmap overrides per-step for generate). |\n| `permission_flag: str` | **✓** | — | Passed to every `claude -p` invocation. |\n| `debug: bool` | **✓** | — | Both pipelines support debug logging. PipelineConfig provides the flag; logging infrastructure is consumer-specific (sprint owns `debug_logger.py`, roadmap provides its own). |\n| `index_path: Path` | — | **✓** | Sprint discovers phases from an index file. Roadmap has no index concept. |\n| `release_dir: Path` | — | **✓** (property alias → `work_dir`) | Sprint code references `release_dir` extensively. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Y4xFSx9UYpKFfXEb9To2kG","type":"tool_result","content":"   600→        self.work_dir = value\n   601→```\n   602→\n   603→### 13.2 Parallel Subprocess Concurrency Model\n   604→\n   605→**Chosen approach**: `threading.Thread` with a shared `threading.Event` for cross-cancellation.\n   606→\n   607→**Rationale**: ClaudeProcess already uses blocking `subprocess.Popen.wait(timeout=)`. Threads are the natural concurrency primitive for I/O-bound blocking calls. `asyncio` would require rewriting ClaudeProcess to use `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec`, which is invasive and risks sprint regression. `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` adds abstraction without benefit — we need exactly 2 threads with cross-cancellation, not a pool.\n   608→\n   609→**Signal handling**: `SignalHandler.shutdown_requested` is already a boolean flag checked in the poll loop. Both threads check it. On SIGINT, both threads' ClaudeProcess instances are terminated. The existing pattern is thread-safe (boolean reads are atomic in CPython; the flag is set from the signal handler on the main thread and read from worker threads).\n   610→\n   611→**Cross-cancellation**: A `threading.Event` (`cancel_event`) is shared between the two generate threads. When one thread's step fails after retry exhaustion, it calls `cancel_event.set()`. The other thread checks `cancel_event.is_set()` in its subprocess poll loop alongside `shutdown_requested`.\n   612→\n   613→**Timeout enforcement**: Each thread enforces its own step timeout independently via `time.monotonic()` deadline — identical to the existing sprint poll loop pattern.\n   614→\n   615→**Gate aggregation**: The main thread joins both worker threads, then checks both results. If either result is not PASS, the pipeline halts.\n   616→\n   617→```python\n   618→def _run_parallel_steps(\n   619→    steps: list[Step],\n   620→    config: PipelineConfig,\n   621→    run_step: StepRunner,\n   622→    cancel_check: Callable[[], bool],\n   623→) -> list[StepResult]:\n   624→    \"\"\"Run steps concurrently. Returns when all complete or one fails.\n   625→\n   626→    Cross-cancellation: if any step fails after retry, a shared Event\n   627→    is set, causing remaining steps to terminate their subprocesses.\n   628→    \"\"\"\n   629→    cancel_event = threading.Event()\n   630→    results: list[StepResult | None] = [None] * len(steps)\n   631→\n   632→    def _worker(idx: int, step: Step):\n   633→        def combined_cancel() -> bool:\n   634→            return cancel_check() or cancel_event.is_set()\n   635→\n   636→        result = _execute_single_step(step, config, run_step, combined_cancel)\n   637→        results[idx] = result\n   638→        if result.status != StepStatus.PASS:\n   639→            cancel_event.set()  # signal other threads to abort\n   640→\n   641→    threads = [\n   642→        threading.Thread(target=_worker, args=(i, s), daemon=True)\n   643→        for i, s in enumerate(steps)\n   644→    ]\n   645→    for t in threads:\n   646→        t.start()\n   647→    for t in threads:\n   648→        t.join()\n   649→\n   650→    return [r for r in results if r is not None]\n   651→```\n   652→\n   653→**Failure propagation sequence**:\n   654→1. generate-A fails gate on attempt 2 → `cancel_event.set()`\n   655→2. generate-B's poll loop sees `cancel_event.is_set()` → calls `proc.terminate()`\n   656→3. generate-B records `StepResult(status=CANCELLED)`\n   657→4. Main thread sees generate-A FAIL → pipeline halts\n   658→5. HALT output shows generate-A as failed, generate-B as cancelled\n   659→\n   660→### 13.3 Prompt Builder Contract\n   661→\n   662→All functions live in `roadmap/prompts.py`. The executor separately appends `--file <path>` for each entry in `step.inputs`. The prompt text references files by description (not path) since `--file` makes content available in context.\n   665→\n   666→```python\n   667→# roadmap/prompts.py\n   668→\n   669→from pathlib import Path\n   670→from typing import Literal\n   671→from ..pipeline.models import AgentSpec\n   672→\n   673→\n   674→def build_extract_prompt(spec_file: Path) -> str:\n   675→    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'extract'.\n   676→\n   677→    Instructs Claude to read the provided specification and produce\n   678→    extraction.md with YAML frontmatter containing functional_requirements,\n   679→    complexity_score, and complexity_class.\n   680→    \"\"\"\n   681→\n   682→def build_generate_prompt(agent: AgentSpec, extraction_path: Path) -> str:\n   683→    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'generate-{agent.id}'.\n   684→\n   685→    Instructs Claude to read the extraction document and generate a\n   686→    complete project roadmap. Threads are the natural concurrency primitive for I/O-bound blocking calls. `asyncio` would require rewriting ClaudeProcess to use `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec`, which is invasive and risks sprint regression. `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` adds abstraction without benefit — we need exactly 2 threads with cross-cancellation, not a pool.\n\n**Signal handling**: `SignalHandler.shutdown_requested` is already a boolean flag checked in the poll loop. Both threads check it. On SIGINT, both threads' ClaudeProcess instances are terminated. The existing pattern is thread-safe (boolean reads are atomic in CPython; the flag is set from the signal handler on the main thread and read from worker threads).\n\n**Cross-cancellation**: A `threading.Event` (`cancel_event`) is shared between the two generate threads. When one thread's step fails after retry exhaustion, it calls `cancel_event.set()`. The other thread checks `cancel_event.is_set()` in its subprocess poll loop alongside `shutdown_requested`.\n\n**Timeout enforcement**: Each thread enforces its own step timeout independently via `time.monotonic()` deadline — identical to the existing sprint poll loop pattern.\n\n**Gate aggregation**: The main thread joins both worker threads, then checks both results. If either result is not PASS, the pipeline halts.\n\n```python\ndef _run_parallel_steps(\n    steps: list[Step],\n    config: PipelineConfig,\n    run_step: StepRunner,\n    cancel_check: Callable[[], bool],\n) -> list[StepResult]:\n    \"\"\"Run steps concurrently. Returns when all complete or one fails.\n\n    Cross-cancellation: if any step fails after retry, a shared Event\n    is set, causing remaining steps to terminate their subprocesses.\n    \"\"\"\n    cancel_event = threading.Event()\n    results: list[StepResult | None] = [None] * len(steps)\n\n    def _worker(idx: int, step: Step):\n        def combined_cancel() -> bool:\n            return cancel_check() or cancel_event.is_set()\n\n        result = _execute_single_step(step, config, run_step, combined_cancel)\n        results[idx] = result\n        if result.status != StepStatus.PASS:\n            cancel_event.set()  # signal other threads to abort\n\n    threads = [\n        threading.Thread(target=_worker, args=(i, s), daemon=True)\n        for i, s in enumerate(steps)\n    ]\n    for t in threads:\n        t.start()\n    for t in threads:\n        t.join()\n\n    return [r for r in results if r is not None]\n```\n\n**Failure propagation sequence**:\n1. generate-A fails gate on attempt 2 → `cancel_event.set()`\n2. generate-B's poll loop sees `cancel_event.is_set()` → calls `proc.terminate()`\n3. generate-B records `StepResult(status=CANCELLED)`\n4. Main thread sees generate-A FAIL → pipeline halts\n5. HALT output shows generate-A as failed, generate-B as cancelled\n\n### 13.3 Prompt Builder Contract\n\nAll functions live in `roadmap/prompts.py`. Each is a **pure function**: takes concrete values, returns `str`, performs no I/O or subprocess calls (NFR-04).\n\nThe returned string is passed to `claude -p \"<prompt>\"`. The executor separately appends `--file <path>` for each entry in `step.inputs`. The prompt text references files by description (not path) since `--file` makes content available in context.\n\n```python\n# roadmap/prompts.py\n\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom typing import Literal\nfrom ..pipeline.models import AgentSpec\n\n\ndef build_extract_prompt(spec_file: Path) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'extract'.\n\n    Instructs Claude to read the provided specification and produce\n    extraction.md with YAML frontmatter containing functional_requirements,\n    complexity_score, and complexity_class.\n    \"\"\"\n\ndef build_generate_prompt(agent: AgentSpec, extraction_path: Path) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'generate-{agent.id}'.\n\n    Instructs Claude to read the extraction document and generate a\n    complete project roadmap. The agent's persona is embedded in the\n    prompt as a role instruction. Output: roadmap-{agent.id}.md with\n    frontmatter fields spec_source, complexity_score, primary_persona.\n    \"\"\"\n\ndef build_diff_prompt(variant_a_path: Path, variant_b_path: Path) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'diff'.\n\n    Instructs Claude to compare two roadmap variants and produce\n    diff-analysis.md with frontmatter fields total_diff_points,\n    shared_assumptions_count.\n    \"\"\"\n\ndef build_debate_prompt(\n    diff_path: Path,\n    variant_a_path: Path,\n    variant_b_path: Path,\n    depth: Literal[\"quick\", \"standard\", \"deep\"],\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'debate'.\n\n    Depth controls the number of debate rounds embedded in the prompt:\n      quick    → 1 round  (\"Single focused round...\")\n      standard → 2 rounds (\"Two rounds: initial positions, then rebuttals...\")\n      deep     → 3 rounds (\"Three rounds: positions, rebuttals, final synthesis...\")\n\n    Output: debate-transcript.md with frontmatter fields convergence_score,\n    rounds_completed.\n    \"\"\"\n\ndef build_score_prompt(\n    debate_path: Path,\n    variant_a_path: Path,\n    variant_b_path: Path,\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'score'.\n\n    Instructs Claude to select a base variant and score both against\n    criteria from the debate. Output: base-selection.md with frontmatter\n    fields base_variant, variant_scores.\n    \"\"\"\n\ndef build_merge_prompt(\n    base_selection_path: Path,\n    variant_a_path: Path,\n    variant_b_path: Path,\n    debate_path: Path,\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'merge'.\n\n    Instructs Claude to produce the final merged roadmap using the\n    base variant, incorporating improvements identified in the debate.\n    Output: roadmap.md with frontmatter fields spec_source,\n    complexity_score, adversarial.\n    \"\"\"\n\ndef build_test_strategy_prompt(\n    roadmap_path: Path,\n    extraction_path: Path,\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for step 'test-strategy'.\n\n    Instructs Claude to produce a test strategy for the roadmap.\n    Output: test-strategy.md with frontmatter fields","numLines":150,"startLine":600,"totalLines":1097}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01TVoipd3ZMG2mjctBNhWuEJ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01ALZHBv9U4bh1gcn4hmARYD","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/config/workspace/SuperClaude_Framework/src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/executor.py","content":"\"\"\"Pipeline executor -- generic step sequencer with retry, gates, and parallel dispatch.\n\nComposition-via-callable design: consumers (sprint, roadmap) inject their own\nStepRunner and callbacks. The executor handles step ordering, retry logic,\nparallel dispatch, and state management.\n\nNFR-007: No imports from superclaude.cli.sprint or superclaude.cli.roadmap.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport logging\nimport threading\nfrom datetime import datetime, timezone\nfrom typing import Callable, Protocol\n\nfrom .gates import gate_passed\nfrom .models import PipelineConfig, Step, StepResult, StepStatus\n\n_log = logging.getLogger(\"superclaude.pipeline.executor\")\n\n\nclass StepRunner(Protocol):\n    \"\"\"Callable that executes a single step's subprocess and returns a result.\n\n    The runner is responsible for:\n    - Launching the claude -p subprocess\n    - Waiting for completion (with timeout enforcement)\n    - Returning a StepResult with appropriate status\n\n    The runner is NOT responsible for:\n    - Retry logic (handled by execute_pipeline)\n    - Gate checking (handled by execute_pipeline)\n    - Step ordering (handled by execute_pipeline)\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __call__(\n        self,\n        step: Step,\n        config: PipelineConfig,\n        cancel_check: Callable[[], bool],\n    ) -> StepResult: ...\n\n\ndef execute_pipeline(\n    steps: list[Step | list[Step]],\n    config: PipelineConfig,\n    run_step: StepRunner,\n    on_step_start: Callable[[Step], None] = lambda s: None,\n    on_step_complete: Callable[[Step, StepResult], None] = lambda s, r: None,\n    on_state_update: Callable[[dict], None] = lambda state: None,\n    cancel_check: Callable[[], bool] = lambda: False,\n) -> list[StepResult]:\n    \"\"\"Generic pipeline executor.\n\n    Processes steps in order. Each element in ``steps`` is either:\n    - A single Step (executed sequentially)\n    - A list[Step] (all steps in the list executed in parallel)\n\n    For each step:\n    1. Call on_step_start(step)\n    2. Call run_step(step, config, cancel_check)\n    3. If step has gate criteria: run gate_passed()\n    4. If gate fails and attempts < retry_limit: retry (go to 2)\n    5. If gate fails and attempts exhausted: HALT\n    6. Call on_step_complete(step, result)\n    7.
